<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Queen (band)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Queen</b> are a British <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band formed in London in 1970, originally consisting of <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> (lead vocals, piano), <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a> (guitar, vocals), <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">John Deacon</a> (bass guitar), and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a> (drums, vocals). Queen's earliest works were influenced by <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, but the band gradually ventured into more conventional and radio-friendly works, incorporating further diverse styles into their music.</p>
<p>Before joining Queen, Brian May and Roger Taylor had been playing together in a band named <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile</a> with bassist <a href="/wiki/Tim_Staffell" title="Tim Staffell">Tim Staffell</a>. Freddie Mercury (then known by his birth name of Farrokh "Freddie" Bulsara) was a fan of Smile, and encouraged them to experiment with more elaborate stage and recording techniques after Staffell's departure in 1970. Mercury himself joined the band shortly thereafter, changed the name of the band to "Queen", and adopted his familiar stage name. John Deacon was recruited prior to recording their <a href="/wiki/Queen_(Queen_album)" title="Queen (Queen album)">eponymous debut album</a> in 1973. Queen enjoyed success in the UK with their debut and its follow-up, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_II" title="Queen II">Queen II</a></i> in 1974, but it was the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack" title="Sheer Heart Attack">Sheer Heart Attack</a></i> later in 1974 and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">A Night at the Opera</a></i> in 1975 that gained the band international success. The latter featured "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", which stayed at number one in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> for nine weeks; it charted at number one in several other territories, and gave the band their first top ten hit on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">US Billboard Hot 100</a>. Their 1977 album, <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World_(album)" title="News of the World (album)">News of the World</a></i>, contained two of rock's most recognisable anthems, "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>".</p>
<p>By the early 1980s, Queen were one of the biggest <a href="/wiki/Arena_rock" title="Arena rock">stadium rock</a> bands in the world, with "<a href="/wiki/Another_One_Bites_the_Dust" title="Another One Bites the Dust">Another One Bites the Dust</a>" their best selling single, and their performance at 1985's <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> is regarded as one of the greatest in rock history. In 1991, Mercury died of <a href="/wiki/Bronchopneumonia" title="Bronchopneumonia">bronchopneumonia</a>, a complication of AIDS, and Deacon retired in 1997. Since then, May and Taylor have occasionally performed together, including a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Free_(band)" title="Free (band)">Free</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Company" title="Bad Company">Bad Company</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a> under the name <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a> which ended in May 2009. Since 2011, May and Taylor have collaborated with vocalist <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> under the name of <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert" title="Queen + Adam Lambert">Queen + Adam Lambert</a>. In late 2014, Queen will release a new album, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Forever" title="Queen Forever">Queen Forever</a></i>, featuring vocals from the late Freddie Mercury.</p>
<p>The band have released a total of 18 number one albums, 18 number one singles, and 10 number one DVDs. Estimates of their record sales generally range from 150 million to 300 million records, making them one of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists</a>. They received the Outstanding Contribution to British Music Award from the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> in 1990, and were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 2001.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_days_.281968.E2.80.931974.29">Early days (1968–1974)</span></h3>
<p>In 1968, guitarist Brian May, a student at London's <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College</a>, and bassist <a href="/wiki/Tim_Staffell" title="Tim Staffell">Tim Staffell</a> decided to form a band. May placed an advertisement on the college notice board for a "<a href="/wiki/Mitch_Mitchell" title="Mitch Mitchell">Mitch Mitchell</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker" title="Ginger Baker">Ginger Baker</a> type" drummer; Roger Taylor, a young dental student, auditioned and got the job. The group called themselves <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While attending <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Art_College" title="Ealing Art College">Ealing Art College</a>, Tim Staffell became friends with Farrokh Bulsara, a fellow student who had assumed the English name of Freddie. Bulsara felt that he and the band had the same tastes and soon became a keen fan of Smile. In late 1970, after Staffell left to join the band <a href="/wiki/Humpy_Bong" title="Humpy Bong">Humpy Bong</a>, the remaining Smile members, encouraged by Bulsara, changed their name to "Queen" and continued working together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QueenZoneBiography1970_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-QueenZoneBiography1970-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> When asked about the name, Bulsara explained, "I thought up the name Queen. It's just a name, but it's very regal obviously, and it sounds splendid. It's a strong name, very universal and immediate. It had a lot of visual potential and was open to all sorts of interpretations. I was certainly aware of gay connotations, but that was just one facet of it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QueenZoneBiography1970_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-QueenZoneBiography1970-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The band had a number of bass players during this period who did not fit with the band's chemistry. It was not until February 1971 that they settled on John Deacon and began to rehearse for their first album. They recorded four of their own songs, "Liar", "Keep Yourself Alive", "The Night Comes Down" and "Jesus", for a demo tape; no record companies were interested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QueenZoneBiography1971_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-QueenZoneBiography1971-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also around this time Freddie changed his surname to "Mercury", inspired by the line "Mother Mercury, look what they've done to me" in the song "My Fairy King".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> On 2 July 1971, Queen played their first show in the classic line-up of Mercury, May, Deacon and Taylor at a Surrey college outside London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Having attended art college, Mercury also designed Queen's logo, called the Queen crest, shortly before the release of the band's first album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOGO_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-LOGO-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The logo combines the <a href="/wiki/Zodiac" title="Zodiac">zodiac</a> signs of all four members: two lions for <a href="/wiki/Leo_(astrology)" title="Leo (astrology)">Leo</a> (Deacon and Taylor), a crab for <a href="/wiki/Cancer_(astrology)" title="Cancer (astrology)">Cancer</a> (May), and two <a href="/wiki/Fairy" title="Fairy">fairies</a> for <a href="/wiki/Virgo_(astrology)" title="Virgo (astrology)">Virgo</a> (Mercury).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOGO_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-LOGO-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The lions embrace a stylised letter Q, the crab rests atop the letter with flames rising directly above it, and the fairies are each sheltering below a lion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOGO_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-LOGO-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> There is also a crown inside the Q and the whole logo is over-shadowed by an enormous <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(mythology)" title="Phoenix (mythology)">phoenix</a>. The whole symbol bears a passing resemblance to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom</a>, particularly with the lion supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOGO_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-LOGO-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The original logo, as found on the reverse-side of the first album cover, was a simple line drawing but more intricate colour versions were used on later sleeves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOGO_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-LOGO-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1972 Queen entered discussions with <a href="/wiki/Trident_Studios" title="Trident Studios">Trident Studios</a> after being spotted at De La Lane Studios by <a href="/wiki/John_Anthony_(record_producer)" title="John Anthony (record producer)">John Antony</a> and after discussions were offered a management deal by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Sheffield" title="Norman Sheffield">Norman Sheffield</a> under Neptune Productions, a subsidiary of Trident to manage the band and enable them to use the facilities at Trident to record new material whilst the management search for a record label to sign Queen. This suited both parties at the time as Trident were expanding into management and Queen under the deal were able to make use of the hi-tech recording facilities shared by bands at the time such as <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> to produce new material. However Trident found it difficult to find a label for a band bearing a name with such connotation during the early 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-life_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-life-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 1973, Queen finally under a Trident/EMI deal released their <a href="/wiki/Queen_(Queen_album)" title="Queen (Queen album)">eponymous debut album</a>, an effort influenced by the heavy metal and <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> of the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was received well by critics; Gordon Fletcher of <i>Rolling Stone</i> said "their debut album is superb",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs-queen-review_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-rs-queen-review-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> and Chicago's <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Herald_(Arlington_Heights)" title="Daily Herald (Arlington Heights)">Daily Herald</a></i> called it an "above average debut".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> It drew little mainstream attention, and the lead single "<a href="/wiki/Keep_Yourself_Alive" title="Keep Yourself Alive">Keep Yourself Alive</a>", a Brian May composition, sold poorly. Retrospectively, "Keep Yourself Alive" is cited as the highlight of the album, and in 2008 <i>Rolling Stone</i> ranked it 31st in the "100 Greatest Guitar Songs of All Time", describing it as "an entire album's worth of riffs crammed into a single song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified gold in the UK and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">A sample of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_March_of_the_Black_Queen" title="The March of the Black Queen">The March of the Black Queen</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_II" title="Queen II">Queen II</a></i> (1974). The band's earlier songs (such as this) leaned more towards progressive rock and heavy metal compared to their later work.</div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The group's second LP, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_II" title="Queen II">Queen II</a></i>, was released in 1974, and features rock photographer <a href="/wiki/Mick_Rock" title="Mick Rock">Mick Rock</a>'s iconic image of the band on the cover. This image would be used as the basis for the 1975 "Bohemian Rhapsody" music video production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The album reached number five on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Album_Chart" title="UK Album Chart">British album chart</a> and became the first Queen album to chart in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The Freddie Mercury-written lead single "<a href="/wiki/Seven_Seas_of_Rhye" title="Seven Seas of Rhye">Seven Seas of Rhye</a>" reached number ten in the UK, giving the band their first hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The album is the first real testament to the band's distinctive layered sound, and features long complex instrumental passages, fantasy-themed lyrics, and musical virtuosity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hodkinson_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hodkinson-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Aside from its only single, the album also included the song "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_March_of_the_Black_Queen" title="The March of the Black Queen">The March of the Black Queen</a>", a six-minute epic which lacks a chorus. The <i>Daily Vault</i> described the number as "menacing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Critical reaction was mixed; the <i>Winnipeg Free Press</i>, while praising the band's debut album, described <i>Queen II</i> as a "over-produced monstrosity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Allmusic has described the album as a favourite among the band's hardcore fans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> and it is the first of three Queen albums to feature in the book <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Albums_You_Must_Hear_Before_You_Die" title="1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die">1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1001albums_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-1001albums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sheer_Heart_Attack_to_A_Night_at_the_Opera_.281974.E2.80.931976.29"><i>Sheer Heart Attack</i> to <i>A Night at the Opera</i> (1974–1976)</span></h3>
<p>After the band's six-night stand at New York's <a href="/wiki/Gershwin_Theatre" title="Gershwin Theatre">Uris Theatre</a> in May 1974, Brian May collapsed and was diagnosed as having hepatitis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hodkinson_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hodkinson-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> While recuperating, May was initially absent when the band started work on their third album, but he returned midway through the recording process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarists_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-guitarists-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Released in 1974, <i><a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack" title="Sheer Heart Attack">Sheer Heart Attack</a></i> reached number two in the United Kingdom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> sold well throughout Europe, and went gold in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> It gave the band their first real experience of international success, and was a hit on both sides of the Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The album experimented with a variety of musical genres, including <a href="/wiki/Music_hall" title="Music hall">British music hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, ballads, ragtime, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Caribbean_music_genres" title="List of Caribbean music genres">Caribbean</a>. At this point, Queen started to move away from the progressive tendencies of their first two releases into a more radio-friendly, song-orientated style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMail_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-DMail-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Sheer Heart Attack</i> introduced new sound and melody patterns that would be refined on their next album, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">A Night at the Opera</a></i>.</p>
<p>The single "<a href="/wiki/Killer_Queen" title="Killer Queen">Killer Queen</a>" from <i>Sheer Heart Attack</i> reached number two on the British charts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and became their first US hit, reaching number 12 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> It combines camp, <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville" title="Vaudeville">vaudeville</a>, and British music hall with May's guitar virtuosity. The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Now_I%27m_Here" title="Now I'm Here">Now I'm Here</a>", a more traditional <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a> composition, was a number eleven hit in Britain, while the high speed rocker "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Crazy" title="Stone Cold Crazy">Stone Cold Crazy</a>" featuring May's uptempo riffs is a precursor to <a href="/wiki/Speed_metal" title="Speed metal">speed metal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarists_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-guitarists-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In recent years, the album has received acclaim from music publications: In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)" title="Classic Rock (magazine)">Classic Rock</a></i> ranked it number 28 in "The 100 Greatest British Rock Albums Ever",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and in 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)" title="Mojo (magazine)">Mojo</a></i> ranked it No.88 in "The 100 Records That Changed the World".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> It is also the second of three Queen albums to feature in the book <i>1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1001albums_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-1001albums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1975, the band left for a world tour with each member in <a href="/wiki/Zandra_Rhodes" title="Zandra Rhodes">Zandra Rhodes</a>-created costumes and accompanied with banks of lights and effects. They toured the US as headliners, and played in Canada for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In September, after an acromonious split with Trident, the band negotiated themselves out of their <a href="/wiki/Trident_Studios" title="Trident Studios">Trident Studios</a> contract and searched for new management. One of the options they considered was an offer from <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>'s manager, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Grant_(music_manager)" title="Peter Grant (music manager)">Peter Grant</a>. Grant wanted them to sign with Led Zeppelin's own production company, <a href="/wiki/Swan_Song_Records" title="Swan Song Records">Swan Song Records</a>. The band found the contract unacceptable and instead contacted <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s manager, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Reid_(music)" title="John Reid (music)">John Reid</a>, who accepted the position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In late 1975, Queen recorded and released <i><a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">A Night at the Opera</a></i>, taking its name from the popular <a href="/wiki/Marx_Brothers" title="Marx Brothers">Marx Brothers</a> movie. At the time, it was the most expensive album ever produced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Like its predecessor, the album features diverse musical styles and experimentation with stereo sound. In "<a href="/wiki/The_Prophet%27s_Song" title="The Prophet's Song">The Prophet's Song</a>", an eight-minute epic, the middle section is a <a href="/wiki/Canon_(music)" title="Canon (music)">canon</a>, with simple phrases layered to create a full-choral sound. The Mercury penned ballad, "<a href="/wiki/Love_of_My_Life_(Queen_song)" title="Love of My Life (Queen song)">Love of My Life</a>", featured a harp and overdubbed vocal harmonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was very successful in Britain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and went <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">triple platinum</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The British public voted it the 13th greatest album of all time in a 2004 <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> poll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> It has also ranked highly in international polls; in a worldwide <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness</a> poll, it was voted the 19th greatest of all time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> while an <a href="/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Australian Broadcasting Corporation">ABC</a> poll saw the Australian public vote it the 28th greatest of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>A Night at the Opera</i> has frequently appeared in "greatest albums" lists reflecting the opinions of critics. Among other accolades, it was ranked number 16 in <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q Magazine</a>'s</i> "The 50 Best British Albums Ever" in 2004, and number 11 in <i>Rolling Stone's</i> "The 100 Greatest Albums of All Time" as featured in their Mexican edition in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also placed at No. 230 on <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine's list of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>" in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>A Night at the Opera</i> is the third and final Queen album to be featured in the book <i>1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1001albums_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-1001albums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album also featured the hit single "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", which was number one in the UK for nine weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury's close friend and advisor, <a href="/wiki/Capital_London" title="Capital London">Capital London</a> radio DJ <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Everett" title="Kenny Everett">Kenny Everett</a>, played a pivotal role in giving the single exposure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">third-best-selling single</a> of all time in the UK, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Band_Aid_(band)" title="Band Aid (band)">Band Aid</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Do_They_Know_It%27s_Christmas%3F" title="Do They Know It's Christmas?">Do They Know It's Christmas?</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind_1997" title="Candle in the Wind 1997">Candle in the Wind 1997</a>", and is the best-selling commercial single in the UK. It also reached number nine in the United States (a 1992 re-release reached number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for five weeks).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the only single ever to sell a million copies on two separate occasions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Online_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Online-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> and became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Christmas_number_one_singles_(UK)" title="List of Christmas number one singles (UK)">Christmas number one</a> twice in the UK, the only single ever to do so. "Bohemian Rhapsody" has been voted numerous times the greatest song of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The band decided to make a video to help go with the single and hired Trilion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> a subsidiary of the former management company <a href="/wiki/Trident_Studios" title="Trident Studios">Trident Studios</a>, using new technology to create the video; the result is generally considered to have been the first "true" music video ever produced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstMusicVideo_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FirstMusicVideo-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's first track "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_on_Two_Legs" title="Death on Two Legs">Death on Two Legs</a>" is said to be written by Mercury about Norman Sheffield and the former management at Trident who helped make the video so popular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-life_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-life-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Although other bands, including <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, had made short promotional films or videos of songs prior to this, generally, those were specifically made to be aired on specific television shows. The second single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_My_Best_Friend_(Queen_song)" title="You're My Best Friend (Queen song)">You're My Best Friend</a>", the second song composed by John Deacon, and his first single, peaked at number sixteen in the United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> and went on to become a worldwide Top Ten hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Online_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Online-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The band's <a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_Tour" title="A Night at the Opera Tour">A Night at the Opera Tour</a> began in November 1975, and covered Europe, the United States, Japan, and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_Day_at_the_Races_to_Live_Killers_.281976.E2.80.931979.29"><i>A Day at the Races</i> to <i>Live Killers</i> (1976–1979)</span></h3>
<p>By 1976, Queen were back in the studio recording <i><a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_(album)" title="A Day at the Races (album)">A Day at the Races</a></i>, which is often regarded as a sequel album to <i>A Night at the Opera</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> It again borrowed the name of a <a href="/wiki/Marx_Brothers" title="Marx Brothers">Marx Brothers</a> movie, and its cover was similar to that of <i>A Night at the Opera</i>, a variation on the same Queen Crest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-night_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-night-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The most recognisable of the Marx Brothers, <a href="/wiki/Groucho_Marx" title="Groucho Marx">Groucho Marx</a>, invited Queen to visit him in his Los Angeles home in March 1977; there the band thanked him in person, and performed "<a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)#.22.2739.22" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">'39</a>" <i><a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Musically, <i>A Day at the Races</i> was by both fans' and critics' standards a strong effort, reaching number one in the UK and Japan, and number five in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-night_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-night-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The major hit on the album was "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(Queen_song)" title="Somebody to Love (Queen song)">Somebody to Love</a>", a gospel-inspired song in which Mercury, May, and Taylor multi-tracked their voices to create a 100-voice gospel choir. The song went to number two in the United Kingdom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bhsa_15-7"><a href="#cite_note-bhsa-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and number thirteen on the US singles chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The album also featured one of the band's heaviest songs, Brian May's "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", which became a staple of their live shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During 1976, Queen played one of their most famous gigs, a free concert in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park, London</a>. It set an attendance record, with 150,000 people confirmed in the audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 December 1976, Queen were the intended guests on London's early evening <i>Today</i> programme, but they pulled out at the last-minute, which saw their late replacement on the show, EMI labelmate the <a href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols" title="Sex Pistols">Sex Pistols</a>, give their seminal interview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_Tour" title="A Day at the Races Tour">A Day at the Races Tour</a> in 1977, Queen performed sold-out shows at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>, New York, in February, and <a href="/wiki/Earls_Court_Exhibition_Centre" title="Earls Court Exhibition Centre">Earls Court</a>, London, in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-history-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The band's sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World_(album)" title="News of the World (album)">News of the World</a></i> was released in 1977, which has gone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platinum_album" title="Platinum album">four times platinum</a> in the United States, and twice in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The album contained many songs tailor-made for live performance, including two of rock's most recognisable anthems, "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" and the rock ballad "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>", both of which became enduring international <a href="/wiki/Stadium_anthem" title="Stadium anthem">sports anthems</a>, and the latter reached number four in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alm_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-alm-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen commenced the <a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World_Tour" title="News of the World Tour">News of the World Tour</a> in October 1977, and Robert Hilburn of the <i>Los Angeles Times</i> called this concert tour the band's "most spectacularly staged and finely honed show".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:QueenPerforming1977.jpg"><img alt="l-r: John Deacon, Brian May, and Freddie Mercury seen live in 1978" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="756" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/QueenPerforming1977.jpg/220px-QueenPerforming1977.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/QueenPerforming1977.jpg/330px-QueenPerforming1977.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/QueenPerforming1977.jpg/440px-QueenPerforming1977.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:QueenPerforming1977.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a>, Connecticut in November 1978.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1978, the band released <i><a href="/wiki/Jazz_(Queen_album)" title="Jazz (Queen album)">Jazz</a></i>, which reached number two in the UK and number six on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The album included the hit singles "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Bottomed_Girls" title="Fat Bottomed Girls">Fat Bottomed Girls</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Bicycle_Race" title="Bicycle Race">Bicycle Race</a>" on a double-sided record. Queen rented Wimbledon Stadium for a day to shoot the video, with 65 naked female models hired to stage a nude bicycle race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Reviews of the album in recent years have been more favourable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Another notable track from <i>Jazz</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_Me_Now" title="Don't Stop Me Now">Don't Stop Me Now</a>", provides another example of the band's exuberant vocal harmonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1978, Queen <a href="/wiki/Jazz_Tour" title="Jazz Tour">toured</a> the US and Canada, and spent much of 1979 touring in Europe and Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tour_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-tour-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> They released their first live album, <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Killers" title="Live Killers">Live Killers</a></i>, in 1979; it went <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platinum_album" title="Platinum album">platinum</a> twice in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen also released the very successful single "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_Little_Thing_Called_Love" title="Crazy Little Thing Called Love">Crazy Little Thing Called Love</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Rockabilly" title="Rockabilly">rockabilly</a> inspired song done in the style of <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crazy_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Crazy-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The song made the top 10 in many countries, topped the Australian <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Charts</a> for seven consecutive weeks, and was the band's first number one single in the United States where it topped the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for four weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-5"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Having written the song on guitar and played rhythm on the record, Mercury played rhythm guitar while performing the song live, which was the first time he ever played guitar in concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crazy_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Crazy-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1979, Queen played the opening night at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concert_for_the_People_of_Kampuchea" title="Concert for the People of Kampuchea">Concert for the People of Kampuchea</a> in London, having accepted a request by the event's organiser <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crazy_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-Crazy-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Game_to_The_Works_.281980.E2.80.931984.29"><i>The Game</i> to <i>The Works</i> (1980–1984)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg"><img alt="Queen during a live concert in Norway in 1982" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg/220px-Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg/330px-Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg/440px-Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_12041982_01_800b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen live in Drammen, Norway, during <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Tour" title="The Game Tour">The Game Tour</a>, April 1982.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Queen began their 1980s career with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Game_(Queen_album)" title="The Game (Queen album)">The Game</a></i>. It featured the singles "Crazy Little Thing Called Love" and "<a href="/wiki/Another_One_Bites_the_Dust" title="Another One Bites the Dust">Another One Bites the Dust</a>", both of which reached number one in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbtfh_30-6"><a href="#cite_note-bbtfh-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> After attending a Queen concert in Los Angeles, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> suggested to Mercury backstage that "Another One Bites the Dust" be released as a single, and in October 1980 it spent three weeks at number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The album topped the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> for five weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> and sold over four million copies in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also the first appearance of a synthesiser on a Queen album. Heretofore, their albums featured a distinctive "No Synthesisers!" sleeve note. The note is widely assumed to reflect an anti-synth, pro-"hard"-rock stance by the band,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> but was later revealed by producer <a href="/wiki/Roy_Thomas_Baker" title="Roy Thomas Baker">Roy Thomas Baker</a> to be an attempt to clarify that those albums' multi-layered solos were created with guitars, not synths, as record company executives kept assuming at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sos1995_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-sos1995-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1980, Queen performed three sold-out shows at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-history-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1980, Queen also released <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_Gordon_(album)" title="Flash Gordon (album)">the soundtrack</a> they had recorded for <i><a href="/wiki/Flash_Gordon_(film)" title="Flash Gordon (film)">Flash Gordon</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_1981" title="American Music Awards of 1981">1981 American Music Awards</a> on 30 January, "Another One Bites the Dust" won the award for Favorite Pop/Rock Single, and Queen were nominated for Favorite Pop/Rock Band, Duo, or Group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1981, Queen travelled to South America as part of <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Tour" title="The Game Tour">The Game Tour</a>, and became the first major rock band to play in Latin American stadiums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tour_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-tour-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour included five shows in Argentina, one of which drew the largest single concert crowd in Argentine history with an audience of 300,000 in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> and two concerts at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Morumbi" title="Estádio do Morumbi">Morumbi Stadium</a> in São Paulo, Brazil, where they played to an audience of more than 131,000 people in the first night (then the largest paying audience for a single band anywhere in the world)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> and more than 120,000 people the following night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> In October of the same year, Queen performed for more than 150,000 fans on 9 October at Monterrey (<a href="/wiki/Estadio_Universitario" title="Estadio Universitario">Estadio Universitario</a>) and 17 and 18 at Puebla (Estadio Zaragoza), Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> On 24 and 25 November, Queen played two sell out nights at the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Forum" title="Montreal Forum">Montreal Forum</a>, Quebec, Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> One of Mercury's most notable performances of <i>The Game'</i>s final track, "<a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">Save Me</a>", took place in Montreal, and the concert is recorded in the live album, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Rock_Montreal" title="Queen Rock Montreal">Queen Rock Montreal</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen worked with <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> on the single "<a href="/wiki/Under_Pressure" title="Under Pressure">Under Pressure</a>". The first-time collaboration with another artist was spontaneous, as Bowie happened to drop by the studio while Queen were recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon its release, the song was extremely successful, reaching number one in the UK and featuring at number 31 on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 100 Greatest Songs of the '80s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Later in 1981, Queen released their first <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Queen_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Queen album)">Greatest Hits</a></i>, which showcased the group's highlights from 1974–1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCS_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-BCS-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of best-selling albums in the United Kingdom">best-selling album</a> in UK Chart history, and has spent 450 weeks in the UK Album Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_head_all-time_sales_chart_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_head_all-time_sales_chart-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMS_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-DMS-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The album is certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">eight times platinum</a> in the United States, and has sold over 25 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Taylor became the first member of the band to release his own solo album in 1981, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Fun_in_Space" title="Fun in Space">Fun in Space</a></i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_1984_012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="522" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Queen_1984_012.jpg/220px-Queen_1984_012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Queen_1984_012.jpg/330px-Queen_1984_012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Queen_1984_012.jpg/440px-Queen_1984_012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_1984_012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen on stage in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> on 26 September 1984. Compatible with his performance and compositions, Mercury was also a multi-instrumentalist.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1982, the band released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_Space" title="Hot Space">Hot Space</a></i>, a departure from their trademark seventies sound, this time being a mixture of rock, <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a>, dance, <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the album was recorded in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> during the most turbulent period in the band's history, and Taylor and May lamented the new sound, with both being very critical of the influence Mercury's personal manager Paul Prenter had on the singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> May was also scathing of Prenter, who was Mercury's manager from the early 1980s to 1984, for being dismissive of the importance of radio stations, such as the US networks, and their vital connection between the artist and the community, and for denying them access to Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> The band stopped touring North America after their <a href="/wiki/Hot_Space_Tour" title="Hot Space Tour">Hot Space Tour</a>, as their success there had waned, although they would perform on American television for the only time during the eighth season premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>. Queen left <a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">Elektra Records</a>, their label in the United States, Canada, Japan, Australia, and New Zealand, and signed onto <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>/<a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a>.</p>
<p>After working steadily for over ten years, Queen decided that they would not perform any live shows in 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> During this time, they recorded a new album at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Record_Plant_Studios" title="Record Plant Studios">Record Plant Studios</a>, Los Angeles and <a href="/wiki/Musicland_Studios" title="Musicland Studios">Musicland Studios</a>, Munich, and several members of the band explored side projects and solo work. May released a mini-album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Fleet_Project" title="Star Fleet Project">Star Fleet Project</a></i>, on which he collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Van_Halen" title="Eddie Van Halen">Eddie Van Halen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1984, Queen released their eleventh studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Works_(Queen_album)" title="The Works (Queen album)">The Works</a></i>, which included the successful singles "<a href="/wiki/Radio_Ga_Ga" title="Radio Ga Ga">Radio Ga Ga</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Break_Free" title="I Want to Break Free">I Want to Break Free</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite these hit singles, the album failed to do well in the United States, while in the UK it went triple platinum and remained in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Album_Chart" title="UK Album Chart">album chart</a> for two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>That year, Queen began <a href="/wiki/The_Works_Tour" title="The Works Tour">The Works Tour</a>, the first tour to feature keyboardist <a href="/wiki/Spike_Edney" title="Spike Edney">Spike Edney</a> as an extra live musician. The tour featured nine sold-out dates in October in <a href="/wiki/Bophuthatswana" title="Bophuthatswana">Bophuthatswana</a>, South Africa, at the arena in <a href="/wiki/Sun_City,_North_West" title="Sun City, North West">Sun City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotshotdigital_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-hotshotdigital-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon returning to England, they were the subject of outrage, having played there during the height of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartheid_in_South_Africa" title="Apartheid in South Africa">apartheid</a> and in violation of worldwide <a href="/wiki/Disinvestment_from_South_Africa" title="Disinvestment from South Africa">divestment efforts</a> and a United Nations cultural boycott. The band responded to the critics by stating that they were playing music for fans in that country, and they also stressed that the concerts were played before integrated audiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen donated to a school for the deaf and blind as a philanthropic gesture but were fined by the <a href="/wiki/Musicians%27_Union_(UK)" title="Musicians' Union (UK)">Musicians' Union</a> and placed on the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Blacklisting" title="Blacklisting">blacklisted</a> artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_Aid_and_later_years_.281985.E2.80.931990.29">Live Aid and later years (1985–1990)</span></h3>
<p>In January 1985, the band headlined two nights of the first <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio</a> festival at <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, Brazil, and played in front of over 300,000 people each night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Boston Globe</i> described it as a "mesmerising performance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globe_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-globe-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> A selection of highlights of both nights was released on VHS with the title <i>Queen: Live in Rio</i>, and was later broadcast on MTV in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globe_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-globe-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> In April and May 1985, Queen completed the Works Tour with sold-out shows in Australia and Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Queen were absolutely the best band of the day... they just went and smashed one hit after another... it was the perfect stage for Freddie: the whole world"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —<a href="/wiki/Bob_Geldof" title="Bob Geldof">Bob Geldof</a>, on Queen's performance at <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a>, held at Wembley on 13 July 1985, in front of the biggest-ever TV audience of 1.9 billion, Queen performed some of their greatest hits, during which the sold-out stadium audience of 72,000 people clapped, sang, and swayed in unison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minchin_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minchin-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The show's organisers, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Geldof" title="Bob Geldof">Bob Geldof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midge_Ure" title="Midge Ure">Midge Ure</a>, other musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl" title="Dave Grohl">Dave Grohl</a>, and various music journalists writing for the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i> among others, commented that Queen stole the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_-_Queen_win_greatest_live_gig_poll_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_-_Queen_win_greatest_live_gig_poll-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Mysterious_Mr_Mercury_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Mysterious_Mr_Mercury-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrianMayBiography_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-BrianMayBiography-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> An industry poll in 2005 named it the greatest rock performance of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_-_Queen_win_greatest_live_gig_poll_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_-_Queen_win_greatest_live_gig_poll-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When interviewed for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mojo_Magazine" title="Mojo Magazine">Mojo</a></i> magazine the band said the most amazing sight at Live Aid was to see the audience clapping to "Radio Ga Ga". Brian May stated: "I'd never seen anything like that in my life and it wasn't calculated either. We understood our audience and played to them but that was one of those weird accidents because of the (music) video. I remember thinking 'oh great, they've picked it up' and then I thought 'this is not a Queen audience'. This is a general audience who've bought tickets before they even knew we were on the bill. And they all did it. How did they know? Nobody told them to do it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo.2Fref_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-mojo.2Fref-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The band, now revitalised by the response to Live Aid – a "shot in the arm" Roger Taylor called it,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo.2Fref_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-mojo.2Fref-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> — and the ensuing increase in record sales, ended 1985 by releasing the single "<a href="/wiki/One_Vision" title="One Vision">One Vision</a>", which was the third time after "Stone Cold Crazy" and "Under Pressure" that all four bandmembers received a writing credit for the one song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, a limited-edition boxed set containing all Queen albums to date was released under the title of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Complete_Works_(Queen_album)" title="The Complete Works (Queen album)">The Complete Works</a></i>. The package included previously unreleased material, most notably Queen's non-album single of Christmas 1984, titled "<a href="/wiki/Thank_God_It%27s_Christmas" title="Thank God It's Christmas">Thank God It's Christmas</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In early 1986, Queen recorded the album <i><a href="/wiki/A_Kind_of_Magic" title="A Kind of Magic">A Kind of Magic</a></i>, containing several reworkings of songs written for the fantasy action film <i><a href="/wiki/Highlander_(film)" title="Highlander (film)">Highlander</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highlander_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Highlander-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was very successful, producing a string of hits, including the title track, "<a href="/wiki/A_Kind_of_Magic_(song)" title="A Kind of Magic (song)">A Kind of Magic</a>". Also charting from the album were "<a href="/wiki/Friends_Will_Be_Friends" title="Friends Will Be Friends">Friends Will Be Friends</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" (featuring an orchestra conducted by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kamen" title="Michael Kamen">Michael Kamen</a>), and the <i>de facto</i> theme from <i>Highlander</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Princes_of_the_Universe" title="Princes of the Universe">Princes of the Universe</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In summer of 1986, Queen went on <a href="/wiki/Magic_Tour_(Queen)" title="Magic Tour (Queen)">their final tour</a> with Freddie Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> A sold-out tour in support of <i>A Kind of Magic</i>, once again they hired Spike Edney, leading to him being dubbed the unofficial fifth member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The Magic Tour's highlight was at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> in London and resulted in the live double album, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_at_Wembley" title="Queen at Wembley">Queen at Wembley</a></i>, released on CD and as a live concert DVD, which has gone five times platinum in the US and four times platinum in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen could not book Wembley for a third night, but they did play at <a href="/wiki/Concerts_at_Knebworth_House" title="Concerts at Knebworth House">Knebworth Park</a>. The show sold out within two hours and over 120,000 fans packed the park for what was Queen's final live performance with Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen began the tour at the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A5sunda_Stadium" title="Råsunda Stadium">Råsunda Stadium</a> in Stockholm, Sweden, and during the tour the band performed a <a href="/wiki/Slane_Concert" title="Slane Concert">concert</a> at <a href="/wiki/Slane_Castle" title="Slane Castle">Slane Castle</a>, Ireland, in front of an audience of 95,000, which broke the venue's attendance record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The band also played behind the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> when they performed to a crowd of 80,000 at the <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s_Stadium" title="Ferenc Puskás Stadium">Népstadion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, in what was one of the biggest rock concerts ever held in Eastern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> More than one million people saw Queen on the tour—400,000 in the United Kingdom alone, a record at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotshotdigital_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-hotshotdigital-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After working on various solo projects during 1988 (including Mercury's collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Caball%C3%A9" title="Montserrat Caballé">Montserrat Caballé</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Barcelona_(album)" title="Barcelona (album)">Barcelona</a></i>), the band released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miracle_(album)" title="The Miracle (album)">The Miracle</a></i> in 1989. The album continued the direction of <i>A Kind of Magic</i>, using a pop-rock sound mixed with a few heavy numbers. It spawned the European hits "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Breakthru_(song)" title="Breakthru (song)">Breakthru</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Invisible_Man_(song)" title="The Invisible Man (song)">The Invisible Man</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Scandal_(song)" title="Scandal (song)">Scandal</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/The_Miracle_(song)" title="The Miracle (song)">The Miracle</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Miracle</i> also began a change in direction of Queen's songwriting philosophy. Since the band's beginning, nearly all songs had been written by and credited to a single member, with other members adding minimally. With <i>The Miracle</i>, the band's songwriting became more collaborative, and they vowed to credit the final product only to Queen as a group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qcw_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-qcw-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mercury:_illness.2C_death.2C_and_tribute_.281988.E2.80.931992.29">Mercury: illness, death, and tribute (1988–1992)</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"There was all that time when we knew Freddie was on the way out, we kept our heads down"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —Brian May<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrianQuoteFreddie_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-BrianQuoteFreddie-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>After fans noticed Mercury's increasingly gaunt appearance in 1988, rumours began to spread that Mercury was suffering from AIDS. Mercury flatly denied this, insisting he was merely "exhausted" and too busy to provide interviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The band decided to continue making albums, starting with <i>The Miracle</i> in 1989 and continuing with <i><a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(album)" title="Innuendo (album)">Innuendo</a></i> in 1991. Despite his deteriorating health, the lead singer continued to contribute. For the last two albums made while Mercury was still alive, the band credited all songs to Queen, rather than specific members of the group, freeing them of internal conflict and differences. In 1990, Queen ended their contract with Capitol and signed with <a href="/wiki/Disney_Music_Group" title="Disney Music Group">Disney</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a>, which has since remained the group's music catalogue owner in the United States and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> That same year, Mercury made his final public appearance when he joined the rest of Queen to collect the <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">BRIT Award</a> for Outstanding Contribution to British Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Innuendo</i> was released in early 1991 with an <a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(song)" title="Innuendo (song)">eponymous number 1 UK hit</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> and other charting singles including, "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury was increasingly ill and could barely walk when the band recorded "The Show Must Go On" in 1990. Because of this, May had concerns about whether he was physically capable of singing it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneSingers_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneSingers-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Recalling Mercury's successful performance May states; "he went in and killed it, completely lacerated that vocal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneSingers_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneSingers-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The band's second greatest hits compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_II_(Queen_album)" title="Greatest Hits II (Queen album)">Greatest Hits II</a></i>, followed in October 1991, which is the eighth best-selling album of all time in the UK and has sold 16 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpialbums_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpialbums-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 November 1991, in a prepared statement made on his deathbed, Mercury confirmed that he had AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_1996_179_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_1996_179-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Within 24 hours of the statement, he died of <a href="/wiki/Bronchopneumonia" title="Bronchopneumonia">bronchial pneumonia</a>, which was brought on as a complication of AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> His funeral service on 27 November in <a href="/wiki/Kensal_Green" title="Kensal Green">Kensal Green</a>, West London was private, and held in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrian</a> religious faith of his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FreddieFuneral_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FreddieFuneral-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> "Bohemian Rhapsody" was re-released as a single shortly after Mercury's death, with "<a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">These Are the Days of Our Lives</a>" as the double A-side. The <a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives#Music_video" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">music video</a> for "These Are the Days of Our Lives" contain Mercury's final scenes in front of the camera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> The single went to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_number-one_singles_(UK)" title="List of number-one singles (UK)">number one</a> in the UK, remaining there for five weeks – the only recording to top the Christmas chart twice and the only one to be number one in four different years (1975, 1976, 1991, and 1992).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Initial proceeds from the single – approximately £1,000,000 – were donated to the <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Higgins_Trust" title="Terrence Higgins Trust">Terrence Higgins Trust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avert_-_History_of_HIV_.26_AIDS_in_the_UK_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Avert_-_History_of_HIV_.26_AIDS_in_the_UK-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen's popularity was stimulated in the United States when "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>" was featured in the 1992 comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World_(film)" title="Wayne's World (film)">Wayne's World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard1992_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1992-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Its inclusion helped the song reach number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for five weeks in 1992 (it remained in the Hot 100 for over 40 weeks),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard1992_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1992-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> and won the band an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Award" title="MTV Award">MTV Award</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1992_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1992 MTV Video Music Awards">1992 MTV Video Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Queen" title="Classic Queen">Classic Queen</a></i> also reached number four on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, and is certified three times platinum in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAC_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAC-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard1992_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1992-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Wayne's World</i> footage was used to make a new music video for "Bohemian Rhapsody", with which the band and management were delighted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 April 1992, <a href="/wiki/The_Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert</a> was held at London's <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> to a 72,000-strong crowd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-definitive3_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-definitive3-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> Performers, including <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Plant" title="Robert Plant">Robert Plant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seal_(musician)" title="Seal (musician)">Seal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extreme_(band)" title="Extreme (band)">Extreme</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> performed various Queen songs along with the three remaining Queen members (and <a href="/wiki/Spike_Edney" title="Spike Edney">Spike Edney</a>.) The concert is listed in the <i>Guinness Book of Records</i> as "The largest rock star <a href="/wiki/Benefit_concert" title="Benefit concert">benefit concert</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> as it was televised to over 1.2 billion viewers worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hotshotdigital_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-hotshotdigital-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> and raised over £20,000,000 for AIDS charities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avert_-_History_of_HIV_.26_AIDS_in_the_UK_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-Avert_-_History_of_HIV_.26_AIDS_in_the_UK-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Made_in_Heaven_to_46664_Concert_.281995.E2.80.932003.29"><i>Made in Heaven</i> to 46664 Concert (1995–2003)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="860" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg/220px-Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg/330px-Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg/440px-Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Bronzestatue_rueckansicht.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of Mercury overlooking <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreux" title="Montreux">Montreux</a>, Switzerland.</div>
