</div>
</div>
<p>Queen's last album featuring Mercury, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven" title="Made in Heaven">Made in Heaven</a></i>, was finally released in 1995, four years after his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Featuring tracks such as "<a href="/wiki/Too_Much_Love_Will_Kill_You" title="Too Much Love Will Kill You">Too Much Love Will Kill You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Heaven_for_Everyone" title="Heaven for Everyone">Heaven for Everyone</a>", it was constructed from Mercury's final recordings in 1991, material left over from their previous studio albums and re-worked material from May, Taylor, and Mercury's solo albums. Both stages of recording, before and after Mercury's death, were completed at the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Studios" title="Mountain Studios">band's studio</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreux" title="Montreux">Montreux</a>, Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMH_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMH-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> The album reached No. 1 on the UK charts immediately following its release, and has sold 20 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUAR_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-GUAR-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-definitive2_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-definitive2-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> On 25 November 1996, a statue of Mercury was unveiled in Montreux overlooking <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a>, almost five years to the day since his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMH_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMH-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"You guys should go out and play again. It must be like having a Ferrari in the garage waiting for a driver"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —<a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, on Queen being without a lead singer since the death of Freddie Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicle_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>In 1997, Queen returned to the studio to record "<a href="/wiki/No-One_but_You_(Only_the_Good_Die_Young)" title="No-One but You (Only the Good Die Young)">No-One but You (Only the Good Die Young)</a>", a song dedicated to Mercury and all those that die too soon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> It was released as a bonus track on the <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Rocks" title="Queen Rocks">Queen Rocks</a></i> compilation album later that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 1997, Queen performed "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>" live with Elton John and the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9jart_Ballet" title="Béjart Ballet">Béjart Ballet</a> in Paris on a night Mercury was remembered, and it marked the last performance and public appearance of John Deacon, who chose to retire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The Paris concert was only the second time Queen had played live since Mercury's death, prompting Elton John to urge them to perform again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicle_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicle-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Brian May and Roger Taylor performed together at several award ceremonies and charity concerts, sharing vocals with various guest singers. During this time, they were billed as <i>Queen +</i> followed by the guest singer's name. In 1998, the duo appeared at <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti" title="Luciano Pavarotti">Luciano Pavarotti</a>'s benefit concert with May performing "<a href="/wiki/Too_Much_Love_Will_Kill_You" title="Too Much Love Will Kill You">Too Much Love Will Kill You</a>" with Pavarotti, later playing "Radio Ga Ga", "We Will Rock You", and "We Are the Champions" with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zucchero" title="Zucchero">Zucchero</a>. They again attended and performed at Pavarotti's benefit concert in <a href="/wiki/Modena" title="Modena">Modena</a>, Italy in May 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> Several of the guest singers recorded new versions of Queen's hits under the <i>Queen +</i> name, such as <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Williams" title="Robbie Williams">Robbie Williams</a> providing vocals for "We Are the Champions" for the soundtrack of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Knight%27s_Tale" title="A Knight's Tale">A Knight's Tale</a></i> (2001).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RobbieWATC_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-RobbieWATC-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen-star-hollywood.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="938" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Queen-star-hollywood.jpg/220px-Queen-star-hollywood.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Queen-star-hollywood.jpg/330px-Queen-star-hollywood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Queen-star-hollywood.jpg/440px-Queen-star-hollywood.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen-star-hollywood.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen's star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> at 6358 Hollywood Boulevard.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1999, a <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_III_(Queen_album)" title="Greatest Hits III (Queen album)">Greatest Hits III</a></i> album was released. This featured, among others, "Queen + <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>" on a <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">rap</a> version of "Another One Bites the Dust". A live version of "Somebody to Love" by <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> and a live version of "The Show Must Go On" with <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> were also featured in the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> By this point, Queen's vast amount of record sales made them the second best selling artist in the UK of all time, behind <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-definitive2_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-definitive2-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2002, Queen were awarded the 2,207th star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>, which is located at 6358 Hollywood Blvd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> On 29 November 2003, May and Taylor performed at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/46664_(concerts)" title="46664 (concerts)">46664 Concert</a> hosted by <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> at <a href="/wiki/Green_Point_Stadium" title="Green Point Stadium">Green Point Stadium</a>, Cape Town, to raise awareness of the spread of HIV/AIDS in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAConcert_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAConcert-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> May and Taylor spent time at Mandela's home, discussing how Africa's problems might be approached, and two years later the band was made ambassadors for the 46664 cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAConcert_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAConcert-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queen_.2B_Paul_Rodgers_.282004.E2.80.932009.29">Queen + Paul Rodgers (2004–2009)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg"><img alt="l-r:Paul Rodgers, Roger Taylor, and Brian May live in 2005 for the Queen + Paul Rodgers tour." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="773" data-file-width="1024" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/220px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/330px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/440px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen performing with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a> during their 2005 <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of 2004, May and Taylor announced that they would reunite and return to touring in 2005 with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a> (founder and former lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Free_(band)" title="Free (band)">Free</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Company" title="Bad Company">Bad Company</a>). Brian May's website also stated that Rodgers would be "featured with" Queen as "Queen + Paul Rodgers", not replacing Mercury. The retired John Deacon would not be participating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bmcom_jdr_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-bmcom_jdr-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2004, Queen were among the inaugural inductees into the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a>, and the award ceremony was the first event at which Rodgers joined May and Taylor as vocalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAConcert_169-2"><a href="#cite_note-SAConcert-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2005 and 2006, Queen + Paul Rodgers embarked on a <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">world tour</a>, which was the first time Queen toured since their <a href="/wiki/Magic_Tour_(Queen)" title="Magic Tour (Queen)">last tour</a> with Freddie Mercury in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005Guardian_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-2005Guardian-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> The band's drummer Roger Taylor commented; "We never thought we would tour again, Paul [Rodgers] came along by chance and we seemed to have a chemistry. Paul is just such a great singer. He's not trying to be Freddie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005Guardian_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-2005Guardian-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> The first leg was in Europe, the second in Japan, and the third in the US in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concertography_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-concertography-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen received the inaugural <a href="/wiki/VH1_Rock_Honors" title="VH1 Rock Honors">VH1 Rock Honors</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay_Events_Center" title="Mandalay Bay Events Center">Mandalay Bay Events Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, Nevada, on 25 May 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concertography_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-concertography-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a> paid homage to the band in performing "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>" to open the ceremony before being joined on stage by May, Taylor, and Paul Rodgers, who played a selection of Queen hits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="901" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG/220px-KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG/330px-KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG/440px-KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KharkovQueenNightConcert01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen + Paul Rodgers concert in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_Square,_Kharkiv" title="Freedom Square, Kharkiv">Kharkiv's Freedom Square</a>, Ukraine, 12 September 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 15 August 2006, Brian May confirmed through his website and fan club that Queen + Paul Rodgers would begin producing their first studio album beginning in October, to be recorded at a "secret location".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen + Paul Rodgers performed at the <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_90th_Birthday_Tribute" title="Nelson Mandela 90th Birthday Tribute">Nelson Mandela 90th Birthday Tribute</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park, London</a> on 27 June 2008, to commemorate Mandela's ninetieth birthday, and again promote awareness of the HIV/AIDS pandemic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> The first Queen + Paul Rodgers album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cosmos_Rocks" title="The Cosmos Rocks">The Cosmos Rocks</a></i>, was released in Europe on 12 September 2008 and in the United States on 28 October 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUAR_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-GUAR-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the release of the album, the band again went on a tour through Europe, opening on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_Square,_Kharkiv" title="Freedom Square, Kharkiv">Kharkiv's Freedom Square</a> in front of 350,000 Ukrainian fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QANDPR_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-QANDPR-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> 12 September concert in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> was later <a href="/wiki/Live_in_Ukraine" title="Live in Ukraine">released on DVD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QANDPR_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-QANDPR-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour then moved to Russia, and the band performed two sold-out shows at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow_arena)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow arena)">Moscow Arena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QROD_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-QROD-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Having completed the first leg of its extensive European tour, which saw the band play 15 sold-out dates across nine countries, the UK leg of the tour sold out within 90 minutes of going on sale and included three London dates, the first of which was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)" title="The O2 Arena (London)">The O<sub>2</sub> Arena</a> on 13 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> The last leg of the tour took place in South America, and included a sold-out concert at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estadio_Jos%C3%A9_Amalfitani" title="Estadio José Amalfitani">Estadio José Amalfitani</a>, Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QROD_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-QROD-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen and Paul Rodgers officially split up without animosity on 12 May 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QNME_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-QNME-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Rodgers stated: "My arrangement with [Queen] was similar to my arrangement with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy</a> [Page] in <a href="/wiki/The_Firm_(rock_band)" title="The Firm (rock band)">The Firm</a> in that it was never meant to be a permanent arrangement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QNME_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-QNME-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Rodgers did not rule out the possibility of working with Queen again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Departure_from_EMI.2C_40th_anniversary_.282009.E2.80.932011.29">Departure from EMI, 40th anniversary (2009–2011)</span></h3>
<p>On 20 May 2009, May and Taylor performed "We Are the Champions" live on the season finale of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> with winner <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a> and runner-up <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> providing a vocal duet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIdol_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIdol-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> In mid-2009, after the split of Queen + Paul Rodgers, the Queen online website announced a new greatest hits compilation named <i><a href="/wiki/Absolute_Greatest" title="Absolute Greatest">Absolute Greatest</a></i>. The album was released on 16 November and peaked at number 3 in the official UK Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> The album contains 20 of Queen's biggest hits spanning their entire career and was released in four different formats: single disc, double disc (with commentary), double disc with feature book, and a <a href="/wiki/LP_record" title="LP record">vinyl record</a>. Prior to its release, a competition was run by Queen online to guess the track listing as a promotion for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 October 2009, May wrote a fanclub letter on his website stating that Queen had no intentions to tour in 2010 but that there was a possibility of a performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letter_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-letter-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> He was quoted as saying, "The greatest debate, though, is always about when we will next play together as Queen. At the moment, in spite of the many rumours that are out there, we do not have plans to tour in 2010. The good news, though, is that Roger and I have a much closer mutual understanding these days—privately and professionally ... and all ideas are carefully considered. Music is never far away from us. As I write, there is an important one-off performance on offer, in the USA, and it remains to be decided whether we will take up this particular challenge. Every day, doors seem to open, and every day, we interact, perhaps more than ever before, with the world outside. It is a time of exciting transition in Rock music and in 'The Business'. It's good that the pulse still beats".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letter_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-letter-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 November 2009, May and Taylor performed "Bohemian Rhapsody" live on the British TV show <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i> alongside the finalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xfactoruk_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-xfactoruk-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:32%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Many of you will have read bits and pieces on the internet about Queen changing record companies and so I wanted to confirm to you that the band have signed a new contract with Universal Music...we would like to thank the EMI team for all their hard work over the years, the many successes and the fond memories, and of course we look forward to continuing to work with EMI Music Publishing who take care of our songwriting affairs. Next year we start working with our new record company to celebrate Queen's 40th anniversary and we will be announcing full details of the plans over the next 3 months. As Brian has already said Queen's next moves will involve 'studio work, computers and live work"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —<a href="/wiki/Jim_Beach" title="Jim Beach">Jim Beach</a>, Queen's Manager, on the change of record label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-label_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-label-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>On 7 May 2010, May and Taylor announced that they were quitting their record label, EMI, after almost 40 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> On 20 August 2010, Queen's manager <a href="/wiki/Jim_Beach" title="Jim Beach">Jim Beach</a> put out a Newsletter stating that the band had signed a new contract with Universal Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-label_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-label-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> During an interview for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hardtalk" title="Hardtalk">Hardtalk</a> on the BBC on 22 September, May confirmed that the band's new deal was with <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island Records</a>, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> For the first time since the late 1980s, Queen's catalogue will have the same distributor worldwide, as their current North American label—<a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a>—is currently distributed by Universal (for a time in the late 1980s, Queen was on EMI-owned <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a> in the US).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 March 2011, which marked the band's 40th anniversary, Queen's first five albums were re-released in the UK and some other territories as remastered deluxe editions (the US versions were released on 17 May).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> The second five albums of Queen's back catalogue were released worldwide on 27 June, with the exception of the US and Canada (27 September).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> The final five were released in the UK on 5 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2011, <a href="/wiki/Jane%27s_Addiction" title="Jane's Addiction">Jane's Addiction</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Perry_Farrell" title="Perry Farrell">Perry Farrell</a> noted that Queen are currently scouting their once former and current live bassist <a href="/wiki/Chris_Chaney" title="Chris Chaney">Chris Chaney</a> to join the band. Farrell stated: "I have to keep Chris away from Queen, who want him and they're not gonna get him unless we're not doing anything. Then they can have him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same month, Paul Rodgers stated he may tour with Queen again in the near future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 2011 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music,_Incorporated" title="Broadcast Music, Incorporated">Broadcast Music, Incorporated</a> (BMI) Awards held in London on 4 October, Queen received the BMI Icon Award in recognition for their airplay success in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Europe Music Awards">2011 MTV Europe Music Awards</a> on 6 November, Queen received the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award_for_Global_Icon" title="MTV Europe Music Award for Global Icon">Global Icon Award</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> presented to Brian May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen closed the awards ceremony, with <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> on vocals, performing "The Show Must Go On", "We Will Rock You" and "We Are the Champions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> The collaboration garnered a positive response from both fans and critics, resulting in speculation about future projects together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonisphere_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sonisphere-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queen_.2B_Adam_Lambert.2C_Queen_Forever_.282011.E2.80.93present.29">Queen + Adam Lambert, <i>Queen Forever</i> (2011–present)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert" title="Queen + Adam Lambert">Queen + Adam Lambert</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg/220px-Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg/330px-Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg/440px-Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen + <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> concert at the <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a>, Boston in July 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 25 and 26 April, May and Taylor appeared on the eleventh series of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_11)" title="American Idol (season 11)">American Idol</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Theatre_L.A._Live" title="Nokia Theatre L.A. Live">Nokia Theatre</a>, Los Angeles, performing a Queen medley with the six finalists on the first show, and the following day performed "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(Queen_song)" title="Somebody to Love (Queen song)">Somebody to Love</a>" with the 'Queen Extravaganza' band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen were scheduled to headline <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonisphere" title="Sonisphere">Sonisphere</a> at <a href="/wiki/Concerts_at_Knebworth_House" title="Concerts at Knebworth House">Knebworth</a> on 7 July 2012 with Adam Lambert<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> before the festival was cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cancelled_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cancelled-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's final concert with Freddie Mercury was in Knebworth in 1986. Brian May commented, "It's a worthy challenge for us, and I'm sure Adam would meet with Freddie's approval."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sonisphere_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sonisphere-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen expressed disappointment at the cancellation and released a statement to the effect that they were looking to find another venue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queenstate_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-queenstate-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> It was later announced that Queen + Adam Lambert would play two shows at the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a>, London on 11 and 12 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> Both shows sold out within 24 hours of tickets going on open sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> A third London date was scheduled for 14 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> On 30 June, Queen + Lambert performed in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, Ukraine at a joint concert with <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> for the Elena Pinchuk ANTIAIDS Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen also performed with Lambert on 3 July 2012 at Moscow's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow)">Olympic Stadium</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> and on 7 July 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Stadion_Miejski_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Stadion Miejski (Wrocław)">Municipal Stadium</a> in Wroclaw, Poland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 August 2012, Queen performed at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> The performance at London's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(London)" title="Olympic Stadium (London)">Olympic Stadium</a> opened with a special remastered video clip of Mercury on stage performing his call and response routine during their 1986 concert at Wembley Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics2012_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics2012-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> Following this, May performed part of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_Rock_(song)" title="Brighton Rock (song)">Brighton Rock</a>" solo before being joined by Taylor and solo artist <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a> for a performance of "We Will Rock You".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics2012_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics2012-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 September 2013, Queen + Adam Lambert performed at the <a href="/wiki/IHeartRadio_Music_Festival" title="IHeartRadio Music Festival">iHeartRadio Music Festival</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Hotel_%26_Casino" title="MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino">MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino</a> in Las Vegas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> On 6 March 2014, the band announced on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> that Queen + Adam Lambert will tour North America in Summer 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> The band will also tour Australia and New Zealand in August/September 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, May and Taylor said that although the tour with Lambert is a limited thing, they are open to him becoming an official member, and cutting new material with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2011, it was announced that Queen will be recording a new album featuring lost demos of Mercury on vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demos_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-Demos-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> May confirmed that he and Taylor are working their way through the band's old material to compile a selection of unreleased songs for the forthcoming album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demos_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-Demos-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> May also revealed that a series of duets that Mercury recorded with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> was to be released in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014, May announced the title of the album to be <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Forever" title="Queen Forever">Queen Forever</a></i>, to be released later in the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queenforever_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-queenforever-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brianrs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="558" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/170px-Brianrs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/255px-Brianrs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/340px-Brianrs.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brianrs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brian May playing his custom made <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The band drew artistic influence from other British rock acts at the time, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slade" title="Slade">Slade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen composed music that drew inspiration from many different genres of music, often with a tongue-in-cheek attitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> The genres they have been associated with include <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Glam_rock" title="Glam rock">glam rock</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_226-2"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_226-3"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_226-4"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_226-5"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_rock" title="Psychedelic rock">psychedelic rock</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blues_rock" title="Blues rock">blues rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance</a>/<a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen also wrote songs that were inspired by genres that are not typically associated with rock, such as <a href="/wiki/Ragtime" title="Ragtime">ragtime</a>, opera, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville" title="Vaudeville">vaudeville</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_music" title="Traditional music">folk</a>.</p>
<p>In 1963, the teenage Brian May and his father <a href="/wiki/Experimental_musical_instrument" title="Experimental musical instrument">custom-built</a> his signature guitar <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>, which was purposely designed to feedback.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> Sonic experimentation figured heavily in Queen's songs. A distinctive characteristic of Queen's music are the vocal harmonies which are usually composed of the voices of May, Mercury, and Taylor best heard on the studio albums <i>A Night at the Opera</i> and <i>A Day at the Races</i>. Some of the ground work for the development of this sound can be attributed to their former producer <a href="/wiki/Roy_Thomas_Baker" title="Roy Thomas Baker">Roy Thomas Baker</a>, and their engineer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Stone_(record_producer)" title="Mike Stone (record producer)">Mike Stone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> Besides vocal harmonies, Queen were also known for <a href="/wiki/Multitrack_recording" title="Multitrack recording">multi-tracking</a> voices to imitate the sound of a large choir through <a href="/wiki/Overdubbing" title="Overdubbing">overdubs</a>. For instance, according to Brian May, there are over 180 vocal overdubs in "Bohemian Rhapsody".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> Many Queen songs were also written with audience participation in mind, such as "We Will Rock You" and "We Are the Champions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwry_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwry-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span></h3>
<p>Queen have been recognised as having made significant contributions to such genres as hard rock,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> and heavy metal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> amongst others. Hence, the band have been cited as an influence by many other musicians. Moreover, like their music, the bands and artists that have claimed to be influenced by Queen are diverse and span different generations, countries, and genres, some of which include, heavy metal; <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queencuttings.com_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-queencuttings.com-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dream_Theater" title="Dream Theater">Dream Theater</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Anthrax_(American_band)" title="Anthrax (American band)">Anthrax</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MP3_David_Lee_Roth_interview_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-MP3_David_Lee_Roth_interview-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> hard rock; <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Van_Halen" title="Van Halen">Van Halen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> glam rock; <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe" title="Mötley Crüe">Mötley Crüe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Darkness_(band)" title="The Darkness (band)">The Darkness</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> alternative rock; <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trent_Reznor" title="Trent Reznor">Trent Reznor</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muse_(band)" title="Muse (band)">Muse</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Smashing_Pumpkins" title="The Smashing Pumpkins">The Smashing Pumpkins</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> pop rock; <a href="/wiki/My_Chemical_Romance" title="My Chemical Romance">My Chemical Romance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> pop; <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen have been cited as a major influence on the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-classical_metal" title="Neo-classical metal">neo-classical metal</a>" genre by Swedish guitarist <a href="/wiki/Yngwie_Malmsteen" title="Yngwie Malmsteen">Yngwie Malmsteen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> recorded a cover version of "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Crazy" title="Stone Cold Crazy">Stone Cold Crazy</a>", which first appeared on the <i><a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A1iy%C3%A1t:_Elektra%27s_40th_Anniversary" title="Rubáiyát: Elektra's 40th Anniversary">Rubáiyát: Elektra's 40th Anniversary</a></i> album in 1990, and won their first Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance in 1991. In the early 1970s, Queen helped spur the <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> genre's evolution by discarding much of its <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> influence;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_239-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queencuttings.com_240-1"><a href="#cite_note-queencuttings.com-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/New_Wave_of_British_Heavy_Metal" title="New Wave of British Heavy Metal">New Wave of British Heavy Metal</a> in addition, they fused the music genre with a <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> sensibility and an increasing emphasis on speed.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<p>In 2002, Queen's "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>" was voted "the UK's favourite hit of all time"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> in a poll conducted by the <i><a href="/wiki/British_Hit_Singles_%26_Albums" title="British Hit Singles &amp; Albums">Guinness World Records British Hit Singles Book</a></i>, and in 2004 the song was inducted into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Hall_of_Fame" title="Grammy Hall of Fame">Grammy Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> Acclaimed for their <a href="/wiki/Arena_rock" title="Arena rock">stadium rock</a>, in 2005 an industry poll ranked Queen's performance at Live Aid in 1985 as the best live act in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMail_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-DMail-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwry_236-1"><a href="#cite_note-wwry-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QueenBestLive_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-QueenBestLive-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, they were also voted the greatest British band in history by <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">BBC Radio 2</a> listeners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QueenBestBritishBand_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-QueenBestBritishBand-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2005, according to the <i>Guinness Book of World Records</i>, Queen albums have spent a total of 1,322 weeks (twenty-six years) on the UK Album Charts, more time than any other musical act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCS_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-BCS-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMS_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-DMS-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 2005, with the release of their live album with Paul Rodgers, Queen moved into third place on the list of acts with the most aggregate time spent on the British record charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, the <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Queen_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Queen album)">Greatest Hits</a></i> album was the all-time best-selling album in UK Chart history, with sales of 5,407,587 copies, over 604,295 more copies than its nearest competitor, the Beatles' <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_head_all-time_sales_chart_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_head_all-time_sales_chart-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Their <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_II_(Queen_album)" title="Greatest Hits II (Queen album)">Greatest Hits II</a></i> album is the seventh best seller, with sales of 3,746,404 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpialbums_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-bpialbums-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The band have released a total of eighteen number one albums, eighteen number one singles, and ten number one DVDs worldwide, making them one of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists</a>. Queen have sold over 150 million records, with some estimates in excess of 300 million records worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwry_236-2"><a href="#cite_note-wwry-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dexp_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-dexp-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesonl_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-timesonl-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QUEEN.E2.80.99S_ROGER_TAYLOR_BBC_NEWS_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-QUEEN.E2.80.99S_ROGER_TAYLOR_BBC_NEWS-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> including 34.5 million albums in the United States alone as of 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> Inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 2001, the band is also the only group in which every member has composed more than one chart-topping single, and all four members of Queen were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_Bio_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hall_Bio-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>" were inducted into the Grammy Hall of Fame,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> and the latter was voted the world's favourite song in a global music poll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen are one of the most bootlegged bands ever, according to Nick Weymouth, who manages the band's official website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MusicWeek_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-MusicWeek-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> A 2001 survey discovered the existence of 12,225 websites dedicated to Queen bootlegs, the highest number for any band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> Bootleg recordings have contributed to the band's popularity in certain countries where Western music is censored, such as Iran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> In a project called <i>Queen: The Top 100 Bootlegs</i>, many of these have been made officially available to download for a nominal fee from Queen's website, with profits going to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mercury_Phoenix_Trust" title="The Mercury Phoenix Trust">Mercury Phoenix Trust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MusicWeek_277-1"><a href="#cite_note-MusicWeek-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked Queen at number 52 on its list of the "100 Greatest Artists of All Time",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> while ranking Mercury the 18th greatest singer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneSingers_139-2"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneSingers-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> and May the twenty-sixth greatest guitarist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen were named 13th on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 100 Greatest Artists of Hard Rock list,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup> and in 2010 were ranked 17th on VH1's 100 Greatest Artists of All Time list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Gigwise" title="Gigwise">Gigwise</a> readers named Queen the best band of past 60 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup> Visitors to <a href="/wiki/Play.com" title="Play.com">Play.com</a> voted them as the best music artist of the last 60 years in their list of "Top 100 Music Artists" in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_other_media">In other media</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_theatre">Musical theatre</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="284" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg/170px-WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg/255px-WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/1a/WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of Mercury at the West End's <a href="/wiki/Dominion_Theatre" title="Dominion Theatre">Dominion Theatre</a> where Queen and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Elton" title="Ben Elton">Ben Elton</a>'s musical <i><a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You_(musical)" title="We Will Rock You (musical)">We Will Rock You</a></i> was performed from 2002 to 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In May 2002, a musical or "rock theatrical" based on the songs of Queen, titled <i><a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You_(musical)" title="We Will Rock You (musical)">We Will Rock You</a></i>, opened at the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_Theatre" title="Dominion Theatre">Dominion Theatre</a> on London's West End.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwry_236-3"><a href="#cite_note-wwry-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> The musical was written by British comedian and author <a href="/wiki/Ben_Elton" title="Ben Elton">Ben Elton</a> in collaboration with Brian May and Roger Taylor, and produced by <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro">Robert De Niro</a>. It has since been staged in many cities around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwry_236-4"><a href="#cite_note-wwry-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the Las Vegas premiere on 8 September 2004, Queen were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Guitar_Center#Hollywood.27s_RockWalk" title="Guitar Center">Hollywood RockWalk</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard" title="Sunset Boulevard">Sunset Boulevard</a>, Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The original London production was scheduled to close on Saturday, 7 October 2006, at the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_Theatre" title="Dominion Theatre">Dominion Theatre</a>, but due to public demand, the show ran until May 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>We Will Rock You</i> has become the longest running musical ever to run at this prime London theatre, overtaking the previous record holder, the <a href="/wiki/Grease_(musical)" title="Grease (musical)"><i>Grease</i> musical</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> Brian May stated in 2008 that they were considering writing a sequel to the musical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup> The musical toured around the UK in 2009, playing at <a href="/wiki/Palace_Theatre,_Manchester" title="Palace Theatre, Manchester">Manchester Palace Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_Empire_Theatre" title="Sunderland Empire Theatre">Sunderland Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Hippodrome" title="Birmingham Hippodrome">Birmingham Hippodrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Hippodrome" title="Bristol Hippodrome">Bristol Hippodrome</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Playhouse" title="Edinburgh Playhouse">Edinburgh Playhouse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The launch of the musical coincided with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II's</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee" title="Golden Jubilee">Golden Jubilee</a>. As part of the Jubilee celebrations, Brian May performed a <a href="/wiki/Guitar_solo" title="Guitar solo">guitar solo</a> of "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brian_may_biography_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-brian_may_biography-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> as featured on Queen's <i>A Night at the Opera</i>, from the roof of <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>. The recording of this performance was used as video for the song on the 30th Anniversary DVD edition of <i>A Night at the Opera</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sean Bovim created "<a href="/wiki/Queen_at_the_Ballet" title="Queen at the Ballet">Queen at the Ballet</a>", a tribute to Mercury, which uses Queen's music as a soundtrack for the show's dancers, who interpret the stories behind tracks such as "Bohemian Rhapsody", "Radio Ga Ga", and "Killer Queen".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen's music also appears in the Off-Broadway production <a href="/wiki/Power_Balladz" title="Power Balladz">Power Balladz</a>, most notably the song "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>", with the show's two performers believing the song was "the apex of artistic achievement in its day".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_realm">Digital realm</span></h3>
<p>In conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, Queen released the computer game <i><a href="/wiki/Queen:_The_eYe" title="Queen: The eYe">Queen: The eYe</a></i> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup> The music itself—tracks from Queen's vast catalogue, in many cases remixed into new instrumental versions—was by and large well received, but the game experience was hampered by poor gameplay. Adding to the problem was an extremely long development time, resulting in graphic elements that already seemed outdated by the time of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Under the supervision of May and Taylor, numerous restoration projects have been under way involving Queen's lengthy audio and video catalogue. DVD releases of their 1986 Wembley concert (titled <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_at_Wembley" title="Queen at Wembley">Live at Wembley Stadium</a></i>), 1982 Milton Keynes concert (<i><a href="/wiki/Queen_on_Fire_%E2%80%93_Live_at_the_Bowl" title="Queen on Fire – Live at the Bowl">Queen on Fire – Live at the Bowl</a></i>), and two Greatest Video Hits (Volumes 1 and 2, spanning the 1970s and 1980s) have seen the band's music remixed into <a href="/wiki/Surround_sound" title="Surround sound">5.1</a> and <a href="/wiki/DTS_(sound_system)" title="DTS (sound system)">DTS</a> <a href="/wiki/Surround_sound" title="Surround sound">surround sound</a>. So far, only two of the band's albums, <i>A Night at the Opera</i> and <i>The Game</i>, have been fully remixed into high-resolution multichannel surround on <a href="/wiki/DVD-Audio" title="DVD-Audio">DVD-Audio</a>. <i>A Night at the Opera</i> was re-released with some revised 5.1 mixes and accompanying videos in 2005 for the 30th anniversary of the album's original release (CD+DVD-Video set). In 2007, a Blu-ray edition of Queen's previously released concerts, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Rock_Montreal" title="Queen Rock Montreal">Queen Rock Montreal</a></i> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a>, was released, marking their first project in 1080p HD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen have been featured multiple times in the <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero">Guitar Hero</a></i> franchise: a cover of "Killer Queen" in the original <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_(video_game)" title="Guitar Hero (video game)">Guitar Hero</a></i>, "We Are The Champions", "Fat Bottomed Girls", and the Paul Rodgers collaboration "C-lebrity" in a track pack for <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_World_Tour" title="Guitar Hero World Tour">Guitar Hero World Tour</a></i>, "Under Pressure" with David Bowie in <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_5" title="Guitar Hero 5">Guitar Hero 5</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> "I Want It All" in <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Van_Halen" title="Guitar Hero: Van Halen">Guitar Hero: Van Halen</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> "Stone Cold Crazy" in <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Metallica" title="Guitar Hero: Metallica">Guitar Hero: Metallica</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> and "Bohemian Rhapsody" in <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Warriors_of_Rock" title="Guitar Hero: Warriors of Rock">Guitar Hero: Warriors of Rock</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup> On 13 October 2009, Brian May revealed there was "talk" going on "behind the scenes" about a dedicated Queen <i>Rock Band</i> game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Queen have also been featured multiple times in the <i>Rock Band</i> franchise: a track pack of 10 songs which are compatible with <i>Rock Band</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_2" title="Rock Band 2">Rock Band 2</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_3" title="Rock Band 3">Rock Band 3</a></i> (three of those are also compatible with <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_Rock_Band" title="Lego Rock Band">Lego Rock Band</a></i>). Their hit "Bohemian Rhapsody" was featured in <i>Rock Band 3</i> with full harmony and keys support. The band also appeared in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_Rock_Band" title="Lego Rock Band">Lego Rock Band</a></i> as playable Lego avatars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2009, <a href="/wiki/Sony_Computer_Entertainment" title="Sony Computer Entertainment">Sony Computer Entertainment</a> released a Queen branded version of the company's karaoke franchise, <i><a href="/wiki/SingStar" title="SingStar">SingStar</a></i>. The game, which is available on <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, is titled <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_in_SingStar_games_(PlayStation_2)" title="List of songs in SingStar games (PlayStation 2)">SingStar Queen</a></i> and has 25 songs on the PS3 and 20 on the PS2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" and other songs by Queen also appear in <i><a href="/wiki/DJ_Hero" title="DJ Hero">DJ Hero</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/One_Vision" title="One Vision">One Vision</a>" was featured on the successful video game <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_IV" title="Grand Theft Auto IV">Grand Theft Auto IV</a></i> on the fictional radio station Liberty Rock Radio 97.8,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup> while "<a href="/wiki/Radio_Ga_Ga" title="Radio Ga Ga">Radio Ga Ga</a>" features on <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_V" title="Grand Theft Auto V">Grand Theft Auto V</a></i> character trailer for Michael and the game's soundtrack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span></h3>
<p>Queen contributed music directly to the films <i><a href="/wiki/Flash_Gordon_(film)" title="Flash Gordon (film)">Flash Gordon</a></i> (1980), with "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_(song)" title="Flash (song)">Flash</a>" as the theme song, and <i><a href="/wiki/Highlander_(film)" title="Highlander (film)">Highlander</a></i> (the original 1986 film),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highlander_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Highlander-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup> with "<a href="/wiki/A_Kind_of_Magic_(song)" title="A Kind of Magic (song)">A Kind of Magic</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_Year_of_Love" title="One Year of Love">One Year of Love</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>", and the theme "<a href="/wiki/Princes_of_the_Universe" title="Princes of the Universe">Princes of the Universe</a>", which was also used as the theme of the <a href="/wiki/Highlander:_The_Series" title="Highlander: The Series"><i>Highlander</i> TV series</a> (1992–1998).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310"><span>[</span>310<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States, "Bohemian Rhapsody" was re-released as a single in 1992 after appearing in the comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World_(film)" title="Wayne's World (film)">Wayne's World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard1992_150-3"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1992-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The single subsequently reached number two on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> (with "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>" as the first track on the single) and helped rekindle the band's popularity in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard1992_150-4"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard1992-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311"><span>[</span>311<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Several films have featured their songs performed by other artists. A version of "Somebody to Love" by <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a> was in the 2004 film <i><a href="/wiki/Ella_Enchanted_(film)" title="Ella Enchanted (film)">Ella Enchanted</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312"><span>[</span>312<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Brittany_Murphy" title="Brittany Murphy">Brittany Murphy</a> also recorded a cover of the same song for the 2006 film <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Feet" title="Happy Feet">Happy Feet</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313"><span>[</span>313<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2001, a version of "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>" was performed by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Broadbent" title="Jim Broadbent">Jim Broadbent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a> in the film musical <i><a href="/wiki/Moulin_Rouge!" title="Moulin Rouge!">Moulin Rouge!</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314"><span>[</span>314<span>]</span></a></sup> The closing credits of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Knight%27s_Tale" title="A Knight's Tale">A Knight's Tale</a></i>, released in 2001, has a version of "We Are the Champions" performed by <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Williams" title="Robbie Williams">Robbie Williams</a> and Queen; the introduction to the same film features "We Will Rock You" played by the medieval audience.</p>
<p>"I Was Born to Love You" was used as the theme song of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_television_drama" title="Japanese television drama">Japanese television drama</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Pride_(TV_series)" title="Pride (TV series)">Pride</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Television" title="Fuji Television">Fuji Television</a> in 2004, starring <a href="/wiki/Takuya_Kimura" title="Takuya Kimura">Takuya Kimura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Y%C5%ABko_Takeuchi" title="Yūko Takeuchi">Yūko Takeuchi</a>. The show's soundtrack also contained other songs by Queen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span>[</span>315<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_Me_Now" title="Don't Stop Me Now">Don't Stop Me Now</a>" has featured in the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> television show <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(current_format)" title="Top Gear (current format)">Top Gear</a></i>, and in 2005 the song was voted as "The Greatest Driving Song Ever" by the shows viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316"><span>[</span>316<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Keeping in a tradition of naming each season's episodes after songs by 1970s rock bands, the eighth and final season of <i><a href="/wiki/That_%2770s_Show" title="That '70s Show">That '70s Show</a></i> had episodes named after Queen songs. "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody_(That_%2770s_Show)" title="Bohemian Rhapsody (That '70s Show)">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>" served as the season premiere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> has made storylines which have featured Queen songs such as "We Will Rock You", "We Are the Champions" (both sung by <a href="/wiki/Homer_Simpson" title="Homer Simpson">Homer</a>), and "You're My Best Friend".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 April 2006, Brian May and Roger Taylor appeared on the American singing contest television show <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>. Each contestant was required to sing a Queen song during that week of the competition. Songs which appeared on the show included "Bohemian Rhapsody", "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Bottomed_Girls" title="Fat Bottomed Girls">Fat Bottomed Girls</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(song)" title="Innuendo (song)">Innuendo</a>". Brian May later criticised the show for editing specific scenes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup> one of which made the group's time with contestant <a href="/wiki/Ace_Young" title="Ace Young">Ace Young</a> look negative, despite it being the opposite. Taylor and May again appeared on the <i>American Idol</i> season 8 finale in May 2009, performing "We Are the Champions" with finalists Adam Lambert and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIdol_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-AIdol-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 November 2009, Brian May and Roger Taylor appeared on the singing contest television show <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">X Factor</a></i> in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-320"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the autumn of 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> featured the fictional high school's show choir singing "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(Queen_song)" title="Somebody to Love (Queen song)">Somebody to Love</a>" as their second act performance in the episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Rhodes_Not_Taken" title="The Rhodes Not Taken">The Rhodes Not Taken</a>". The performance was included on the show's <i><a href="/wiki/Glee:_The_Music,_Volume_1" title="Glee: The Music, Volume 1">Volume 1</a></i> soundtrack CD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321"><span>[</span>321<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2010, the choir performed "Another One Bites the Dust" in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Funk_(Glee)" title="Funk (Glee)">Funk</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322"><span>[</span>322<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2012, the choir performed "We Are the Champions" in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Nationals_(Glee)" title="Nationals (Glee)">Nationals</a>", and the song features in <i><a href="/wiki/Glee:_The_Music,_The_Graduation_Album" title="Glee: The Music, The Graduation Album">The Graduation Album</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2010, Brian May announced in a BBC interview that <a href="/wiki/Sacha_Baron_Cohen" title="Sacha Baron Cohen">Sacha Baron Cohen</a> was to play Mercury in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercury_(film)" title="Mercury (film)">film of the same name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> commented with approval on his singing ability and visual similarity to Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in July 2013, Baron Cohen dropped out of the role due to "creative differences" between him and the surviving band members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326"><span>[</span>326<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2013, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Ben_Whishaw" title="Ben Whishaw">Ben Whishaw</a>, best known for playing <a href="/wiki/Q_(James_Bond)" title="Q (James Bond)">Q</a> in the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Skyfall" title="Skyfall">Skyfall</a></i>, had been chosen to replace Cohen in the role of Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whishaw_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-whishaw-327"><span>[</span>327<span>]</span></a></sup> The motion picture is being written by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Morgan" title="Peter Morgan">Peter Morgan</a>, who had been nominated for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscars</a> for his screenplays <i><a href="/wiki/The_Queen_(film)" title="The Queen (film)">The Queen</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Frost/Nixon_(film)" title="Frost/Nixon (film)">Frost/Nixon</a></i>. The film, which is being co-produced by <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro">Robert De Niro</a>'s <a href="/wiki/TriBeCa_Productions" title="TriBeCa Productions">TriBeCa Productions</a>, will focus on Queen's formative years and the period leading up to the celebrated performance at the <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">1985 Live Aid</a> concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328"><span>[</span>328<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-sos1995-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-sos1995_76-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation journal">Cunningham, Mark (October 1995). <a class="external text" href="http://www.soundonsound.com/sos/1995_articles/oct95/queen.html" rel="nofollow">"AN INVITATION TO THE OPERA: Roy Thomas Baker &amp; Gary Langan: The Making Of Queen's 'Bohemian Rhapsody<span style="padding-right:0.2em;">'</span>"</a>. <i>Sound on Sound</i>. <q>There was no stipulation that we wouldn't have any synths, but the statement 'No synths' was printed on the album sleeves because of peoples' lack of intellect in the ears department. Many people couldn't hear the difference between a multitracked guitar and a synthesiser. We would spend four days multi-layering a guitar solo and then some imbecile from the record company would come in and say, 'I like that synth!'</q></span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AQueen+%28band%29&amp;rft.atitle=AN+INVITATION+TO+THE+OPERA%3A+Roy+Thomas+Baker+%26+Gary+Langan%3A+The+Making+Of+Queen%27s+%27Bohemian+Rhapsody%27&amp;rft.au=Cunningham%2C+Mark&amp;rft.aufirst=Mark&amp;rft.aulast=Cunningham&amp;rft.date=October+1995&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.soundonsound.com%2Fsos%2F1995_articles%2Foct95%2Fqueen.html&amp;rft.jtitle=Sound+on+Sound&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
